## OpenHands Workspace Rules

- The provided working directory is the only submission surface for this evaluation.
- Do not `git clone`, `git init`, or fetch the target repository into the working directory or any of its subdirectories.
- Use MCP to inspect remote code, then create or edit only the files you need directly in the working directory using repository-relative paths.
- The verifier only reads changes from the provided working directory, not from any self-cloned checkout.


# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Onboarding: Cilium Codebase Orientation

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5 (mirror of cilium/cilium)
**Task Type:** Codebase Orientation (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a new engineer joining a team that works on Cilium, a cloud-native networking, observability, and security platform that uses eBPF. Your manager has asked you to spend your first day exploring the codebase and answering key orientation questions so you can hit the ground running.

## Your Task

Explore the Cilium codebase and answer the following questions. Write your answers to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md`.

### Questions

1. **Main Entry Point**: Where does the cilium-agent binary start execution? Identify the main function, how the CLI is initialized, and what dependency injection framework is used to wire components together.

2. **Core Packages**: Identify at least 5 core packages under `pkg/` and describe what each one is responsible for. Focus on the packages that handle networking policy, the datapath, Kubernetes integration, endpoint management, and eBPF maps.

3. **Configuration Loading**: How does the agent load its configuration? Describe the configuration pipeline: what config formats are supported, what library is used for config binding, and What modules/interfaces define the main config struct?

4. **Test Structure**: How are tests organized in this project? Describe at least 3 different testing approaches used (e.g., unit tests, integration tests, privileged tests, BPF tests). Where do end-to-end tests live?

5. **Network Policy Pipeline**: Trace the path of a CiliumNetworkPolicy from CRD definition to eBPF enforcement. Identify at least 4 stages in this pipeline and name the relevant components or packages involved at each stage (e.g., CRD types, K8s watcher, policy repository, endpoint regeneration, BPF map sync).

6. **Adding a New Network Policy Type**: If you needed to add a new type of network policy rule (e.g., a new L7 protocol filter), which packages and files would you need to modify? Describe the sequence of changes required.

## Output Requirements

Write your answers to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` with this structure:

```
# Cilium Codebase Orientation

## 1. Main Entry Point
<Your answer>

## 2. Core Packages
<Your answer>

## 3. Configuration Loading
<Your answer>

## 4. Test Structure
<Your answer>

## 5. Network Policy Pipeline
<Your answer>

## 6. Adding a New Network Policy Type
<Your answer>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Do NOT write any code changes
- Your job is exploration and documentation only
- Be specific — include file paths, package names, function names, and struct names where relevant

* Each action you take is somewhat expensive. Wherever possible, combine multiple actions into a single action, e.g. combine multiple bash commands into one, using sed and grep to edit/view multiple files at once.
* When exploring the codebase, use efficient tools like find, grep, and git commands with appropriate filters to minimize unnecessary operations.
</EFFICIENCY>

<FILE_SYSTEM_GUIDELINES>
* When a user provides a file path, do NOT assume it's relative to the current working directory. First explore the file system to locate the file before working on it.
* If asked to edit a file, edit the file directly, rather than creating a new file with a different filename.
* For global search-and-replace operations, consider using `sed` instead of opening file editors multiple times.
* NEVER create multiple versions of the same file with different suffixes (e.g., file_test.py, file_fix.py, file_simple.py). Instead:
  - Always modify the original file directly when making changes
  - If you need to create a temporary file for testing, delete it once you've confirmed your solution works
  - If you decide a file you created is no longer useful, delete it instead of creating a new version
* Do NOT include documentation files explaining your changes in version control unless the user explicitly requests it

The file is complete and well-formed. Here is a summary of everything that was researched and written.

---

## `onboarding.md` — What Was Written and Why

The document at `/workspace/onboarding.md` answers all six orientation questions with precise file references drawn directly from the codebase. Here is a concise summary of the findings:

---

### Q1 — Main Entry Point
**`daemon/main.go`** is the binary entry point. Its three-line `main()` builds a dependency graph with `hive.New(cmd.Agent)` and then calls `cmd.Execute(cmd.NewAgentCmd(agentHive))`. The `NewAgentCmd` function (in `daemon/cmd/root.go`) creates a Cobra command that fires three `OnInitialize` hooks — `option.InitConfig()`, `initDaemonConfig()`, `initLogging()` — before calling `h.Run()` to start all cells. The DI framework is Cilium's own `github.com/cilium/hive/cell`; the top-level cell (`cmd.Agent`) is composed of `Infrastructure + ControlPlane + datapath.Cell` in `daemon/cmd/cells.go`.

---

### Q2 — Core Packages
The ~80 packages in `pkg/` are grouped into five functional clusters: **policy engine** (`pkg/policy/api/`, `pkg/policy/`, `pkg/policy/k8s/`), **datapath/BPF** (`pkg/maps/policymap/`, `pkg/datapath/`), **endpoint lifecycle** (`pkg/endpoint/`, `pkg/endpointmanager/`), **Kubernetes integration** (`pkg/k8s/`, `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/`), and **identity/IPCache** (`pkg/identity/`, `pkg/ipcache/`).

---

### Q3 — Configuration Loading
Config is loaded in `option.InitConfig()` (`pkg/option/config.go` ~L4215) using **Viper**. Precedence (high → low): CLI flags → `CILIUM_`-prefixed env vars → `--config-dir` directory (one file per key, used for Kubernetes ConfigMap mounts) → `--config` YAML file. All settings land in the `option.DaemonConfig` struct (~500 fields, ~L1401), which is populated once a
... (truncated)

{
  "command": "create",
  "file_text": "# Cilium v1.16.5 \u2014 Engineering Onboarding Guide\n\nThis document answers six orientation questions for engineers joining the Cilium\nproject. All file paths are relative to the repository root\n(`github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`).\n\n---\n\n## 1. Main Entry Point\n\n### Where execution begins\n\n```\ndaemon/main.go\n```\n\n`main()` is a three-liner:\n\n```go\n// daemon/main.go\nagentHive := hive.New(cmd.Agent)          // build the dependency graph\ncmd.Execute(cmd.NewAgentCmd(agentHive))   // parse CLI flags and run\n```\n\n### What `NewAgentCmd` does\n\n`daemon/cmd/root.go` constructs a `cobra.Command` whose `RunE` calls\n`h.Run()` (the hive lifecycle). Before the command runs, Cobra's\n`OnInitialize` hooks fire three setup functions in order:\n\n| Hook | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `option.InitConfig()` | Load config file, config-dir, and env vars via Viper |\n| `initDaemonConfig()` | Apply daemon-specific defaults and validate options |\n| `initLogging()` | Configure the logrus logger |\n\n### The hive / dependency-injection framework\n\nCilium uses its own DI framework (`github.com/cilium/hive/cell`). The\ntop-level cell is defined in `daemon/cmd/cells.go`:\n\n```go\n// daemon/cmd/cells.go\nvar Agent = cell.Module(\"agent\", \"Cilium Agent\",\n    Infrastructure,   // k8s client, resource watchers, metrics, \u2026\n    ControlPlane,     // policy, endpoint manager, ipcache, \u2026\n    datapath.Cell,    // BPF loader, maps, orchestrator\n)\n```\n\nEach sub-cell declares its dependencies as constructor parameters; the\nframework wires them together at startup and calls `OnStart`/`OnStop`\nlifecycle hooks in dependency order.\n\n### Startup sequence (summary)\n\n```\ndaemon/main.go\n  \u2514\u2500 hive.New(cmd.Agent)          \u2190 build DI graph\n  \u2514\u2500 cmd.Execute(NewAgentCmd)\n       \u2514\u2500 cobra.OnInitialize\n            \u251c\u2500 option.InitConfig()\n            \u251c\u2500 initDaemonConfig()\n            \u2514\u2500 initLogging()\n       \u2514\u2500 h.Run()                  \u2190 start all cells in order\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Core Packages\n\nThe `pkg/` directory contains ~80 packages. The most important ones for\nunderstanding the agent are:\n\n### Policy engine\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/policy/api/` | Public API types: `Rule`, `IngressRule`, `EgressRule`, `PortRule`, `L7Rules`, `L4Proto`, selectors |\n| `pkg/policy/` | In-memory policy repository (`Repository`), compiled L4 filter (`L4Filter`, `L4Policy`), map-state (`MapState`), distillery |\n| `pkg/policy/k8s/` | Kubernetes watchers that translate CNP/CCNP/KNP objects into `api.Rules` and call `PolicyAdd` |\n| `pkg/policy/directory/` | Watches a local directory for static CNP YAML files |\n\n### Datapath / BPF\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/maps/policymap/` | Go wrapper for the per-endpoint `cilium_policy_<id>` BPF LPM map |\n| `pkg/maps/ctmap/` | Connection-tracking BPF maps |\n| `pkg/maps/ipcache/` | IP-to-identity BPF map |\n| `pkg/maps/lbmap/` | Load-balancer BPF maps |\n| `pkg/datapath/linux/` | Linux-specific datapath implementation |\n| `pkg/datapath/loader/` | BPF program compilation and loading |\n\n### Endpoint lifecycle\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/endpoint/` | `Endpoint` struct, policy regeneration (`policy.go`), BPF sync (`bpf.go`) |\n| `pkg/endpointmanager/` | Registry of all local endpoints |\n\n### Kubernetes integration\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/k8s/` | Kubernetes client, informers, service cache |\n| `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/` | CRD Go types: `CiliumNetworkPolicy`, `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy`, etc. |\n| `pkg/k8s/resource/` | Generic typed resource watcher (used by policy watchers) |\n| `pkg/k8s/synced/` | Tracks which API groups have been synced |\n\n### Identity and IPCache\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/identity/` | Numeric identity allocation and label-to-identity mapping |\n| `pkg/ipcache/` | IP-prefix \u2192 identity cache; drives BPF ipcache map updates |\n\n### Configuration and utilities\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/option/` | `DaemonConfig` struct and `InitConfig()` |\n| `pkg/labels/` | Label types and selectors |\n| `pkg/eventqueue/` | Serialized event queue used for policy reactions |\n| `pkg/testutils/` | Test helpers (`PrivilegedTest`, `IntegrationTest`) |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Configuration Loading\n\n### Sources and precedence (highest \u2192 lowest)\n\n1. **CLI flags** (cobra/pflag) \u2014 e.g. `--enable-ipv6`\n2. **Environment variables** \u2014 same names with `CILIUM_` prefix and\n   hyphens replaced by underscores, e.g. `CILIUM_ENABLE_IPV6`\n3. **Config directory** (`--config-dir`) \u2014 each file in the directory is\n   treated as a key whose content is the value; this is how Kubernetes\n   `ConfigMap` mounts are consumed\n4. **Config file** (`--config`) \u2014 a YAML file; default path is\n   `/etc/cilium/cilium-config`\n\nAll four sources are unified by **Viper** (`github.com/spf13/viper`).\n\n### Code path\n\n```\noption.InitConfig()                    // pkg/option/config.go ~L4215\n  \u251c\u2500 viper.SetEnvPrefix(\"CILIUM\")\n  \u251c\u2500 viper.AutomaticEnv()\n  \u251c\u2500 viper.SetConfigFile(configFile)   // --config flag\n  \u251c\u2500 viper.ReadInConfig()\n  \u2514\u2500 for each file in configDir:\n       viper.Set(filename, content)    // --config-dir / ConfigMap\n```\n\n### The config struct\n\n`option.DaemonConfig` (defined at `pkg/option/config.go` ~L1401) is a\nlarge struct (~500 fields) that holds every tuneable. It is populated\nonce during startup and then read-only for the lifetime of the process.\nFlags are registered in `daemon/cmd/daemon_main.go` via\n`flags.StringVar`, `flags.BoolVar`, etc., and bound to Viper with\n`viper.BindPFlags`.\n\n### Runtime feature flags\n\nMany features are gated by fields on `DaemonConfig`, for example:\n\n```go\nif p.config.EnableK8sNetworkPolicy {\n    knpEvents = p.networkPolicies.Events(ctx)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Test Structure\n\nCilium uses three distinct test tiers, each with different requirements\nand invocation methods.\n\n### Tier 1 \u2014 Standard unit tests\n\nPlain `go test ./...`. No special environment needed. These live\nalongside the code they test (e.g. `pkg/policy/api/rule_test.go`,\n`pkg/policy/repository_test.go`). They use `github.com/stretchr/testify`\nfor assertions.\n\n```bash\ngo test ./pkg/policy/...\n```\n\n### Tier 2 \u2014 Privileged tests (require root / Linux capabilities)\n\nTests that exercise real network namespaces, BPF maps, or netlink calls\ncall `testutils.PrivilegedTest(t)` as their first line:\n\n```go\n// daemon/cmd/daemon_privileged_test.go\nfunc Test_removeOldRouterState(t *testing.T) {\n    testutils.PrivilegedTest(t)   // skips unless PRIVILEGED_TESTS=1\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe helper (in `pkg/testutils/privileged.go`) skips the test unless the\n`PRIVILEGED_TESTS` environment variable is set:\n\n```bash\nPRIVILEGED_TESTS=1 go test ./daemon/cmd/...\n```\n\nSimilarly, integration tests guard themselves with\n`testutils.IntegrationTest(t)` and require `INTEGRATION_TESTS=1`.\n\nBPF-level unit tests live in `test/bpf/` and are written in C\n(`unit-test.c`), compiled and run via `test/bpf/Makefile`.\n\n### Tier 3 \u2014 Control-plane integration tests\n\nLocated in `test/controlplane/`, these are full agent integration tests\nthat spin up a real (but in-process) agent against a fake Kubernetes API\nserver. They follow a **\"k8s objects in, mock datapath state out\"**\npattern:\n\n- Test cases register themselves via `init()` calling `suite.AddTestCase`.\n- Each test uses `suite.NewControlPlaneTest` to start the agent, then\n  applies/deletes Kubernetes objects and asserts on the resulting\n  datapath state.\n- Many use **golden files** for expected output; update them with\n  `-update`:\n\n```bash\ngo test ./test/controlplane                          # run all\ngo test ./test/controlplane -test.v -update          # regenerate golden files\ngo test ./test/controlplane -test.v -debug           # verbose log output\n```\n\n### Tier 4 \u2014 End-to-end tests\n\nFull cluster tests live in `test/k8s/` and `test/runtime/`. They require\na running Kubernetes cluster (typically provisioned with `kind`) and are\ndriven by the Ginkgo framework. These are run in CI but not locally\nduring normal development.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Network Policy Pipeline\n\nA `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP) applied to the cluster travels through\nseven stages before it affects packet forwarding.\n\n### Stage 1 \u2014 Kubernetes API watch\n\n`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go` \u2014 `policyWatcher.watchResources(ctx)`\n\nA single goroutine selects over four event channels:\n\n| Channel | Source |\n|---|---|\n| `cnpEvents` | `CiliumNetworkPolicy` resources |\n| `ccnpEvents` | `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy` resources |\n| `knpEvents` | Kubernetes native `NetworkPolicy` (if `EnableK8sNetworkPolicy=true`) |\n| `cidrGroupEvents` | `CiliumCIDRGroup` resources |\n\n### Stage 2 \u2014 Reference resolution\n\n`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go` \u2014 `resolveCiliumNetworkPolicyRefs()`\n\nBefore the policy is imported, two types of external references are\ninlined:\n\n- **CIDRGroupRef** \u2192 expanded to a concrete `CIDRSet` by looking up the\n  `CiliumCIDRGroup` cache (`resolveCIDRGroupRef`)\n- **ToServices** \u2192 translated to `ToCIDRSet` entries using the service\n  endpoint cache (`resolveToServices`)\n\n### Stage 3 \u2014 Parse to `api.Rules`\n\n`pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go` \u2014 `CiliumNetworkPolicy.Parse()`\n\nThe CRD object's `Spec`/`Specs` fields (typed as `*api.Rule` /\n`api.Rules`) are validated, namespace-scoped, and returned as a slice of\n`*api.Rule`. For native Kubernetes `NetworkPolicy`, the equivalent\nfunction is `pkg/k8s/network_policy.go:ParseNetworkPolicy()`.\n\n### Stage 4 \u2014 Policy repository update\n\n`daemon/cmd/policy.go` \u2014 `Daemon.PolicyAdd()` \u2192 `Daemon.policyAdd()`\n\n`PolicyAdd` is the public entry point (implements the `PolicyManager`\ninterface). It enqueues a `PolicyAddEvent` onto the daemon's event queue\nto serialize concurrent updates. Inside `policyAdd`:\n\n1. Acquires `d.policy.Mutex` (the repository lock).\n2. Calls `d.policy.ReplaceByResourceLocked(rules, resourceID)` (for CNP)\n   or `d.policy.AddListLocked(rules)` (for gRPC API).\n3. Calls `addedRules.FindSelectedEndpoints(...)` to determine which\n   endpoints are affected.\n4. Releases the lock and enqueues a `PolicyReactionEvent`.\n\n### Stage 5 \u2014 Endpoint regeneration\n\n`daemon/cmd/policy.go` \u2014 `PolicyReactionEvent.Handle()` \u2192\n`reactToRuleUpdates()`\n\nThe reaction event:\n\n1. Bumps the policy revision counter for endpoints not directly affected.\n2. Calls `endpoint.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)` for each affected\n   endpoint (asynchronously).\n3. Calls `ipcache.UpsertPrefixes()` to allocate identities for any new\n   CIDR prefixes referenced by the rules.\n\n### Stage 6 \u2014 Per-endpoint policy recompilation\n\n`pkg/endpoint/policy.go` \u2014 `Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()`\n\nFor each affected endpoint, the policy engine:\n\n1. Walks the policy repository and evaluates which rules select this\n   endpoint's identity labels.\n2. Compiles the matching rules into an `L4Policy` (ingress + egress\n   `L4Filter` maps keyed by port/protocol).\n3. Expands each `L4Filter` into a `MapState` \u2014 a flat map of\n   `(identity, port, protocol, direction) \u2192 allow/deny`.\n\n### Stage 7 \u2014 BPF map synchronization\n\n`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` \u2014 `Endpoint.syncPolicyMap()`\n\nThe computed `MapState` is diffed against the currently realized state.\nOnly the delta is written to the per-endpoint BPF LPM map\n(`cilium_policy_<endpointID>`, implemented in\n`pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go`). The BPF datapath then uses this map\nfor every packet decision via tail-call programs referenced from\n`cilium_call_policy` and `cilium_egresscall_policy`.\n\n### Pipeline diagram\n\n```\nK8s API server\n    \u2502  CiliumNetworkPolicy event\n    \u25bc\npkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go          watchResources()\n    \u2502  onUpsert / onDelete\n    \u25bc\npkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go   resolveCiliumNetworkPolicyRefs()\n    \u2502  CIDRGroupRef + ToServices expansion\n    \u25bc\npkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go   CiliumNetworkPolicy.Parse()\n    \u2502  \u2192 []api.Rule\n    \u25bc\ndaemon/cmd/policy.go               Daemon.PolicyAdd()\n    \u2502  policy repository lock \u2192 ReplaceByResourceLocked()\n    \u2502  FindSelectedEndpoints()\n    \u25bc\ndaemon/cmd/policy.go               PolicyReactionEvent.Handle()\n    \u2502  endpoint.RegenerateIfAlive()\n    \u2502  ipcache.UpsertPrefixes()\n    \u25bc\npkg/endpoint/policy.go             Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()\n    \u2502  \u2192 MapState (desired)\n    \u25bc\npkg/endpoint/bpf.go                Endpoint.syncPolicyMap()\n    \u2502  diff desired vs realized\n    \u25bc\npkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go    cilium_policy_<id> BPF map\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nBPF datapath (packet verdict)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Adding a New Network Policy Type\n\nTo introduce a new policy type (for example, a hypothetical\n`CiliumDNSEgressPolicy` CRD), you need to touch files across four layers.\nBelow is the complete checklist with the canonical existing type as a\nreference.\n\n### Layer 1 \u2014 CRD Go types\n\n**Reference:** `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go`\n\n1. Create `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/<yourtype>_types.go` with the\n   Kubernetes object struct (embed `metav1.TypeMeta` + `metav1.ObjectMeta`).\n2. Add a `Spec *api.Rule` (or `Specs api.Rules`) field to hold the policy\n   rules.\n3. Implement a `Parse() (api.Rules, error)` method that validates the\n   spec and returns `[]api.Rule`. Use\n   `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/utils/utils.go:ParseToCiliumRule()` to\n   namespace-scope selectors.\n4. Run `make generate` to regenerate `zz_generated.deepcopy.go` and\n   `zz_generated.deepequal.go`.\n\n### Layer 2 \u2014 API rule types (if adding new match fields)\n\n**Reference:** `pkg/policy/api/l4.go`, `pkg/policy/api/http.go`\n\nIf your policy type introduces new match criteria (e.g. a new L7\nprotocol):\n\n1. Add a new field to `L7Rules` in `pkg/policy/api/l4.go`:\n   ```go\n   type L7Rules struct {\n       HTTP  []PortRuleHTTP  `json:\"http,omitempty\"`\n       Kafka []kafka.PortRule `json:\"kafka,omitempty\"`\n       DNS   []PortRuleDNS   `json:\"dns,omitempty\"`\n       MyProto []PortRuleMyProto `json:\"myProto,omitempty\"` // new\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n2. Create `pkg/policy/api/myproto.go` with the `PortRuleMyProto` struct\n   and a `Sanitize() error` method.\n3. Update `L7Rules.Len()` to count the new field.\n4. Add a new `L7ParserType` constant in `pkg/policy/l4.go` and handle it\n   in the `switch` that assigns `l4.L7Parser` (~line 876).\n\n### Layer 3 \u2014 Kubernetes watcher\n\n**Reference:** `pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go`,\n`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go`\n\n1. Add a `resource.Resource[*YourType]` field to `policyWatcher`.\n2. In `watchResources()`, subscribe to events for your new resource type\n   and add a `case` to the `select` loop.\n3. Implement `onUpsertYourType()` and `onDeleteYourType()` handlers\n   (following the pattern of `onUpsert` / `onDelete` for CNP):\n   - Call `yourObj.Parse()` to get `api.Rules`.\n   - Call `p.policyManager.PolicyAdd(rules, &policy.AddOptions{...})`.\n4. Add a `yourTypeSynced atomic.Bool` field and set it on the `Sync`\n   event.\n\n### Layer 4 \u2014 Cell wiring\n\n**Reference:** `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go`\n\n1. Add your new `resource.Resource[*YourType]` as a parameter to the\n   `newPolicyWatcher` constructor so the hive framework injects it.\n2. Register the new API group with `k8sAPIGroups.AddAPI(...)` and\n   `k8sResourceSynced.BlockWaitGroupToSyncResources(...)` so the agent\n   waits for the initial list before declaring itself ready.\n\n### Layer 5 \u2014 CRD registration\n\n**Reference:** `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/register.go`\n\n1. Add your new type to the `SchemeBuilder` so it is registered with the\n   Kubernetes API machinery.\n2. Add the CRD YAML manifest under `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/crds/`.\n\n### Layer 6 \u2014 Tests\n\n1. **Unit tests** \u2014 add `pkg/policy/api/myproto_test.go` to test\n   `Sanitize()` and validation logic.\n2. **Watcher tests** \u2014 add\n   `pkg/policy/k8s/<yourtype>_test.go` following the pattern of\n   `cilium_network_policy_test.go`.\n3. **Control-plane integration test** \u2014 add a new test case under\n   `test/controlplane/` using `suite.AddTestCase` and\n   `suite.NewControlPlaneTest`. Provide input YAML fixtures and golden\n   output files for the expected datapath state.\n\n### Summary of files to create or modify\n\n| File | Action |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/<yourtype>_types.go` | **Create** \u2014 CRD struct + `Parse()` |\n| `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/register.go` | **Modify** \u2014 register new type |\n| `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/crds/<yourtype>.yaml` | **Create** \u2014 CRD manifest |\n| `pkg/policy/api/l4.go` | **Modify** \u2014 add field to `L7Rules` (if new L7 protocol) |\n| `pkg/policy/api/<yourproto>.go` | **Create** \u2014 new `PortRule` struct (if new L7 protocol) |\n| `pkg/policy/l4.go` | **Modify** \u2014 add `L7ParserType` constant and switch case |\n| `pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go` | **Modify** \u2014 add resource field + event channel |\n| `pkg/policy/k8s/<yourtype>.go` | **Create** \u2014 `onUpsert` / `onDelete` handlers |\n| `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go` | **Modify** \u2014 inject new resource into constructor |\n| `test/controlplane/<yourtype>/` | **Create** \u2014 integration test fixtures |\n",

They require\n   242\ta running Kubernetes cluster (typically provisioned with `kind`) and are\n   243\tdriven by the Ginkgo framework. These are run in CI but not locally\n   244\tduring normal development.\n   245\t\n   246\t---\n   247\t\n   248\t## 5. Network Policy Pipeline\n   249\t\n   250\tA `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP) applied to the cluster travels through\n   251\tseven stages before it affects packet forwarding.\n   252\t\n   253\t### Stage 1 \u2014 Kubernetes API watch\n   254\t\n   255\t`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go` \u2014 `policyWatcher.watchResources(ctx)`\n   256\t\n   257\tA single goroutine selects over four event channels:\n   258\t\n   259\t| Channel | Source |\n   260\t|---|---|\n   261\t| `cnpEvents` | `CiliumNetworkPolicy` resources |\n   262\t| `ccnpEvents` | `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy` resources |\n   263\t| `knpEvents` | Kubernetes native `NetworkPolicy` (if `EnableK8sNetworkPolicy=true`) |\n   264\t| `cidrGroupEvents` | `CiliumCIDRGroup` resources |\n   265\t\n   266\t### Stage 2 \u2014 Reference resolution\n   267\t\n   268\t`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go` \u2014 `resolveCiliumNetworkPolicyRefs()`\n   269\t\n   270\tBefore the policy is imported, two types of external references are\n   271\tinlined:\n   272\t\n   273\t- **CIDRGroupRef** \u2192 expanded to a concrete `CIDRSet` by looking up the\n   274\t  `CiliumCIDRGroup` cache (`resolveCIDRGroupRef`)\n   275\t- **ToServices** \u2192 translated to `ToCIDRSet` entries using the service\n   276\t  endpoint cache (`resolveToServices`)\n   277\t\n   278\t### Stage 3 \u2014 Parse to `api.Rules`\n   279\t\n   280\t`pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go` \u2014 `CiliumNetworkPolicy.Parse()`\n   281\t\n   282\tThe CRD object's `Spec`/`Specs` fields (typed as `*api.Rule` /\n   283\t`api.Rules`) are validated, namespace-scoped, and returned as a slice of\n   284\t`*api.Rule`. For native Kubernetes `NetworkPolicy`, the equivalent\n   285\tfunction is `pkg/k8s/network_policy.go:ParseNetworkPolicy()`.\n   286\t\n   287\t### Stage 4 \u2014 Policy repository update\n   288\t\n   289\t`daemon/cmd/policy.go` \u2014 `Daemon.PolicyAdd()` \u2192 `Daemon.policyAdd()`\n   290\t\n   291\t`PolicyAdd` is the public entry point (implements the `PolicyManager`\n   292\tinterface). It enqueues a `PolicyAddEvent` onto the daemon's event queue\n   293\tto serialize concurrent updates. Inside `policyAdd`:\n   294\t\n   295\t1. Acquires `d.policy.Mutex` (the repository lock).\n   296\t2. Calls `d.policy.ReplaceByResourceLocked(rules, resourceID)` (for CNP)\n   297\t   or `d.policy.AddListLocked(rules)` (for gRPC API).\n   298\t3. Calls `addedRules.FindSelectedEndpoints(...)` to determine which\n   299\t   endpoints are affected.\n   300\t4. Releases the lock and enqueues a `PolicyReactionEvent`.\n   301\t\n   302\t### Stage 5 \u2014 Endpoint regeneration\n   303\t\n   304\t`daemon/cmd/policy.go` \u2014 `PolicyReactionEvent.Handle()` \u2192\n   305\t`reactToRuleUpdates()`\n   306\t\n   307\tThe reaction event:\n   308\t\n   309\t1. Bumps the policy revision counter for endpoints not directly affected.\n   310\t2. Calls `endpoint.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)` for each affected\n   311\t   endpoint (asynchronously).\n   312\t3. Calls `ipcache.UpsertPrefixes()` to allocate identities for any new\n   313\t   CIDR prefixes referenced by the rules.\n   314\t\n   315\t### Stage 6 \u2014 Per-endpoint policy recompilation\n   316\t\n   317\t`pkg/endpoint/policy.go` \u2014 `Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()`\n   318\t\n   319\tFor each affected endpoint, the policy engine:\n   320\t\n   321\t1. Walks the policy repository and evaluates which rules select this\n   322\t   endpoint's identity labels.\n   323\t2. Compiles the matching rules into an `L4Policy` (ingress + egress\n   324\t   `L4Filter` maps keyed by port/protocol).\n   325\t3. Expands each `L4Filter` into a `MapState` \u2014 a flat map of\n   326\t   `(identity, port, protocol, direction) \u2192 allow/deny`.\n   327\t\n   328\t### Stage 7 \u2014 BPF map synchronization\n   329\t\n   330\t`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` \u2014 `Endpoint.syncPolicyMap()`\n   331\t\n   332\tThe computed `MapState` is diffed against the currently realized state.\n   333\tOnly the delta is written to the per-endpoint BPF LPM map\n   334\t(`cilium_policy_<endpointID>`, implemented in\n   335\t`pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go`). The BPF datapath then uses this map\n   336\tfor every packet decision via tail-call programs referenced from\n   337\t`cilium_call_policy` and `cilium_egresscall_policy`.\n   338\t\n   339\t### Pipeline diagram\n   340\t\n   341\t```\n   342\tK8s API server\n   343\t    \u2502  CiliumNetworkPolicy event\n   344\t    \u25bc\n   345\tpkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go          watchResources()\n   346\t    \u2502  onUpsert / onDelete\n   347\t    \u25bc\n   348\tpkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go   resolveCiliumNetworkPolicyRefs()\n   349\t    \u2502  CIDRGroupRef + ToServices expansion\n   350\t    \u25bc\n   351\tpkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go   CiliumNetworkPolicy.Parse()\n   352\t    \u2502  \u2192 []api.Rule\n   353\t    \u25bc\n   354\tdaemon/cmd/policy.go               Daemon.PolicyAdd()\n   355\t    \u2502  policy repository lock \u2192 ReplaceByResourceLocked()\n   356\t    \u2502  FindSelectedEndpoints()\n   357\t    \u25bc\n   358\tdaemon/cmd/policy.go               PolicyReactionEvent.Handle()\n   359\t    \u2502  endpoint.RegenerateIfAlive()\n   360\t    \u2502  ipcache.UpsertPrefixes()\n   361\t    \u25bc\n   362\tpkg/endpoint/policy.go             Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()\n   363\t    \u2502  \u2192 MapState (desired)\n   364\t    \u25bc\n   365\tpkg/endpoint/bpf.go                Endpoint.syncPolicyMap()\n   366\t    \u2502  diff desired vs realized\n   367\t    \u25bc\n   368\tpkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go    cilium_policy_<id> BPF map\n   369\t    \u2502\n   370\t    \u25bc\n   371\tBPF datapath (packet verdict)\n   372\t```\n   373\t\n   374\t---\n   375\t\n   376\t## 6. Adding a New Network Policy Type\n   377\t\n   378\tTo introduce a new policy type (for example, a hypothetical\n   379\t`CiliumDNSEgressPolicy` CRD), you need to touch files across four layers.\n   380\tBelow is the complete checklist with the canonical existing type as a\n   381\treference.\n   382\t\n   383\t### Layer 1 \u2014 CRD Go types\n   384\t\n   385\t**Reference:** `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go`\n   386\t\n   387\t1. Create `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/<yourtype>_types.go` with the\n   388\t   Kubernetes object struct (embed `metav1.TypeMeta` + `metav1.ObjectMeta`).\n   389\t2. Add a `Spec *api.Rule` (or `Specs api.Rules`) field to hold the policy\n   390\t   rules.\n   391\t3. Implement a `Parse() (api.Rules, error)` method that validates the\n   392\t   spec and returns `[]api.Rule`. Use\n   393\t   `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/utils/utils.go:ParseToCiliumRule()` to\n   394\t   namespace-scope selectors.\n   395\t4. Run `make generate` to regenerate `zz_generated.deepcopy.go` and\n   396\t   `zz_generated.deepequal.go`.\n   397\t\n   398\t### Layer 2 \u2014 API rule types (if adding new match fields)\n   399\t\n   400\t**Reference:** `pkg/policy/api/l4.go`, `pkg/policy/api/http.go`\n   401\t\n   402\tIf your policy type introduces new match criteria (e.g. a new L7\n   403\tprotocol):\n   404\t\n   405\t1. Add a new field to `L7Rules` in `pkg/policy/api/l4.go`:\n   406\t   ```go\n   407\t   type L7Rules struct {\n   408\t       HTTP  []PortRuleHTTP  `json:\"http,omitempty\"`\n   409\t       Kafka []kafka.PortRule `json:\"kafka,omitempty\"`\n   410\t       DNS   []PortRuleDNS   `json:\"dns,omitempty\"`\n   411\t       MyProto []PortRuleMyProto `json:\"myProto,omitempty\"` // new\n   412\t       ...\n   413\t   }\n   414\t   ```\n   415\t2. Create `pkg/policy/api/myproto.go` with the `PortRuleMyProto` struct\n   416\t   and a `Sanitize() error` method.\n   417\t3. Update `L7Rules.Len()` to count the new field.\n   418\t4. Add a new `L7ParserType` constant in `pkg/policy/l4.go` and handle it\n   419\t   in the `switch` that assigns `l4.L7Parser` (~line 876).\n   420\t\n   421\t### Layer 3 \u2014 Kubernetes watcher\n   422\t\n   423\t**Reference:** `pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go`,\n   424\t`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go`\n   425\t\n   426\t1. Add a `resource.Resource[*YourType]` field to `policyWatcher`.\n   427\t2. In `watchResources()`, subscribe to events for your new resource type\n   428\t   and add a `case` to the `select` loop.\n   429\t3. Implement `onUpsertYourType()` and `onDeleteYourType()` handlers\n   430\t   (following the pattern of `onUpsert` / `onDelete` for CNP):\n   431\t   - Call `yourObj.Parse()` to get `api.Rules`.\n   432\t   - Call `p.policyManager.PolicyAdd(rules, &policy.AddOptions{...})`.\n   433\t4. Add a `yourTypeSynced atomic.Bool` field and set it on the `Sync`\n   434\t   event.\n   435\t\n   436\t### Layer 4 \u2014 Cell wiring\n   437\t\n   438\t**Reference:** `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go`\n   439\t\n   440\t1.
